$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Bromination with NBS in TBAB;
5-Bromo-6-aminocoumarin; Typical Procedure (Table 1, Entry 13)
6-Aminocoumarin (342 mg, 2.12 mmol) was added to solid TBAB (0.4 g) with
stirring and when the resulting mixture became a clean melt, NBS (380 mg,
2.13 mmol) was added. This was heated to 100 °C in a closed glass vial
and then kept at that temperature for 4 h (TLC monitoring). H2O (4 mL)
was then added to remove succinimide followed by extraction with a
minimum amount of EtOAc. The organic extract, after washing with brine,
drying (Na2SO4) and careful removal of solvent, gave one product
exclusively along with TBAB. The crude product was purified by filtration
through a short pad of silica gel using CH2Cl2-light petroleum ether
mixture (1:1) as the eluent. Shining bright yellow crystals of
5-bromo-6-aminocoumarin were obtained. TBAB was recovered almost
quantitatively from later fractions as shining white crystals, which was
reused without any decrease of yield of bromo products. Entry 1, yield
90%.

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General procedure for bromination and
iodination of aromatic substrates To a mixture of aromatic substrate (1
mmol) and appropriate amount of NH4Br (Table 1) in AcOH (or MeCN for
anilines) (4 mL) was added
trans-3,5-dihydroperoxy-3,5-dimethyl-1,2-dioxolane 1 (0.5 mmol) and the
mixture was stirred at room temperature for an appropriate time (Table
1). After completion of the reaction as monitored by TLC (n-hexane/
EtOAc; 2:1), 1 M aqueous solution of Na2SO3 (3 mL) was added to quench
the reaction and stirring was continued for further 10 min. Then, the
reaction mixture was diluted with distilled water (15 mL). The
precipitated product was filtered and washed with water (2 x 3 mL) to
yield almost pure product. Table 1, Entry 3, yield 90%. Mp (°C): Found =
88-90. Reported [60, 62] = 85-86.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):NOTES
$DATUM green chemistry, regioselective, safety
(trans-3,5-dihydroperoxy-3,5-dimethyl-1,2-dioxolane is potentially
explosive), product depends on stoichiometry, alternative preparation

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: GENERAL PROCEDURE A solution of substrate (5
mmol), copper(II) bromide (5 mmol) and potassium dichromate (5.5 mmol) in
glacial acetic acid (5 mmol) in a 100 ml round-bottomed flask equipped
with a magnetic stirrer was prepared. The reaction mixture was allowed to
stirred at ambient temprature for an approperiate time (Table I). The
progress of the reaction was monitored by TLC (eluent hexane/ethyl
acetate, 10/1). After completion of the reaction, dichloromethane (50 mL)
was added to the mixture and the reaction mixture was filtered. The
filtrate was washed with water (50 mL x 2) and then with sodium carbonate
solution (50 mL x 2). The organic layer after separation was dried over
anhydrous sodium sulfate and filtered. The solvent was evaporated. The
resulting crude material was purified on a silica gel plate with
appropriate solvent. Pure bromo compounds were obtained in 65-95% yields
(Table I). 2,4,6-Tribromo phenol, yield 90%.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):REFERENCE(1):TITLE
$DATUM A new method for the oxybromination of aromatic compounds with copper(II)
bromide and potassium dichromate
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):REFERENCE(1):AUTHOR
$DATUM Badri, Rashid; Shushizadeh, Mohammad Reza
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):REFERENCE(1):CITATION
$DATUM Phosphorus, Sulfur and Silicon and the Related Elements (2005), 180(2),
533-536

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM Bromination of aromatic compounds with bromine: To perfluorohexane (1.5
mL) in a test tube was slowly added Br2 (10 mmol). After 5 minutes, when
all the bromine had settled down to the bottom of the tube, a solution of
one of the aromatic compounds 1a-d (2 mmol) in dichloromethane (1.5 mL)
was carefully added to form the uppermost layer. The test tube was
covered with A1 foil and kept at room temperature for 1-3 days. After
this period, the remaining two layers were separated and the
dichloromethane layer was washed with aqueous sodium thiosulfate
solution, then with water, and then it was dried over MgSO4 followed by
evaporation of the solvent. The products 2a-d were purified by
chromatography over silica gel using 5 % ether in hexane for 2a-b and 10%
ether in hexane for 2c-d as eluent. 2, 4, 6-Tribromo phenol4b,c,e,h (2a):
1H NMR (CDCl3, 300 MHz): δ 5.87 (s, 1H), 7.58 (s, 2H) 13C NMR (CDCl3,
75.5 MHz): δ 110.6, 112.8, 134.4, 149.1

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General Procedure for the Preparation of
Compounds 3a-m: Aryl halide (2 mmol for entries 1-8 and 10-14, 1 mmol for
entry 9 in Table 1), substituted phenol (3 mmol) and
(S)-N-methylpyrrolidine-2-carboxamide hydrochloride (66 mg, 0.4 mmol)
were added to a flask with potassium phosphate (607 mg, 4.4 mmol) and DMF
containing 3% H2O (3 mL), and the mixture was stirred for 30 min at r.t.
Under a nitrogen atmosphere CuI (40 mg, 0.2 mmol) was added to the flask.
The flask was immersed in an oil bath, and the reaction mixture was
stirred at 110 °C for the reaction time shown in Table 1. The reaction
mixture was then allowed to cool to r.t., diluted with EtOAc (10 mL) and
filtered, and the filtrate was concentrated under vacuum to give the
crude product. Purification by column chromatography on silica gel
(hexane-EtOAc, 15:1 → 50:1) afforded the desired pure. 3k. Yield 90 %.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):REFERENCE(1):TITLE
$DATUM Highly efficient copper-catalyzed O-arylation using readily available
(S)-N-methylpyrrolidine-2-carboxamide as the ligand

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General Procedure for Iodination of Anisole in
Ionic Liquid I2 (227mg, 1 mmol) and NaBO3·4H2O (310 mg, 1 mmol) were
taken in a mortar and ground well. This powdered mixture was then added
to a mixture of anisole (214mg, 2 mmol) and 2 ml of [bmim]BF4. The
resulting reaction mixture was stirred at room temperature for the time
specified in Table 2. After the reaction reached maximum conversion (as
indicated by GC), the crude product was isolated by extracting it with
ether. The extracts were washed successively with saturated sodium
thiosulphate solution, brine, and water, and passed through anhydrous
Na2SO4. The crude product was purified on silica-gel column
chromatography using hexane-ethyl acetate as eluent. After the crude
product was extracted from the reaction mixture with diethyl ether, the
ionic liquid was reused for subsequent runs, and the previously mentioned
procedure was followed. Table 2. Sr. no. 7, yield 90%.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):REFERENCE(1):TITLE
$DATUM Regioselective iodination of arenes using iodine/NaBO3.4H2O system in
ionic liquid

Manikrao M.

$DATUM 12) Rh2(OAc)4-Catalyzed Decomposition of Diazoacetonyl-substituted Cyclic
Ethers. General Procedure. Under N2 atmosphere, a mixture of Rh2(OAc)4 (3
mol%) and protic nucleophile (usually MeOH, 1.2-1.3 mol equivalent to the
diazoketone) were dissolved in CH2Cl2 (15 ml), to which was added slowly
a CH2Cl2 solution (10 ml) of diazoketone (3 mmol) over 10 min. After
diazoketone was consumed, the reaction was quenched by saturated aqueous
NaHCO3, the organic layer was washed with water and dried over anhydrous
MgSO4. Solvent was removed and the residue was subjected to flash
chromatography to isolate product(s). 13) Ethyl Phenyl
2-(5-Hexen-1-yloxy)malonate (4g). The reaction of 1f in the presence of

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: III - Direct Arylation versus Biaryl Ether
Formation It is interesting to note that the direct arylation of the
multi-functionalized 2-pyrimidinone with p-tolyl and phenyl boronic acids
produced the unexpected biaryl ethers (9a and 10a) (C-O bond formation)
as the minor side products along with the desired biaryl products (9 and
10). To confirm their structures, the identical biaryl ethers 9a and 10a
were alternatively prepared via our previous phosphonium coupling
condition for the direct CO bond formation by using the corresponding
phenols (Kang, F.-A., et al. J. Org. Chem. 2005, 70, 1957). The reason
for the biaryl ether formation on this substrate was unclear, and neither
C-C nor C-O bond formation was observed in the absence of PyBroP.
4-Methyl-2-phenoxy-6-phenyl-pyrimidine-5-carboxylic acid ethyl ester
(Compound 10a): White solid; yield 90% 1H NMR (CDCl3) δ 1.06, (t, 3H, J =
7.0 Hz), 2.57 (s, 3H), 4.17 (q, 2H, J = 7.0 Hz), 7.25 (m, 3H), 7.42 (m,
5H), 7.59 (m, 2H); 13C NMR (CDCl3) δ 13,6, 22.8, 61.8, 121.0, 121.6,
125.2, 128.3, 128.4, 129.4, 130.3, 137.3, 152.8, 163.9, 166.6, 168.1,
169.2; MS m/e (MH+) 335.

$DATUM General Procedure (2a-b): 2-Substituted-3-formylquinoline Equimolar
amounts of the phenol or benzenethiol (20 mmol) and potassium hydroxide
(20 mmol) were dissolved in dimethyl sulfoxide (10 mL). After dissolution
of the reactants, a solution of 1 (20 mmol) was added dropwise to
dimethyl sulfoxide. The mixture was refluxed for 6 h (85 °C-90 °C) and
monitored by TLC until the reaction was completed. After cooling, the
reaction mixture was poured into ice water and neutralized with dilute
hydrochloric acid to pH 5-6. Compound no.: 2a; Yellow; Yield: 90%.
C17H15NO2; mol.wt.: 265.11; IR (cm-1): 1706 (C=O), 1617 (C=N), 1238
(C-O-C); 1H NMR (CDCl3): 9.56 (s, 1H, -CHO), 8.26 (s, 1H, quinolin-H4),
8.13-7.23 (m, 9H, Ar-H); MS, m/z(M+): 265 (M+), 221, 192, 165, 143, 128,
101,91, 78

$DATUM General procedure for the synthesis of
2-phenoxy-3-quinilinecarboxaldehyde (2) A solution of
2-chloro-3-quinilinecarboxaldehyde 1 (3.82 g, 20 mmol) dissolved in
dimethyl sulfoxide (35 mL)was added to a mixture of phenol (1.88 g, 20
mmol) and potassium hydroxide (2.76 g, 20 mmol) in DMSO(15 mL) and the
reaction mixture was heated to 85-90 °C for 6 h. The reaction mixture was
cooled to room temperature and then poured onto ice-water. The pHwas
adjusted to 6-7 with dilute hydrochloric acid. The resulting pale yellow
precipitate was filtered, washed with H2O and dried. The crude product
was recrystallized from EtOAc. Yellow solid (90%). mp 150-151 °C; FT-IR ν
1706 (C=O), 1617 (C=N), 1238 (C-O-C) cm−1; 1HNMR δ 9.56 (s, 1H, -CHO),
8.26 (s, 1H, quinolin-H4), 8.13-7.23 (m, 9H, ArH);MS (EI):m/z 249 (M+).
Anal.Calcd. For C16H11NO2: C, 77.10; H, 4.45; N, 5.62; Found: C, 77.06;
H, 4.42; N, 5.58.

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General Procedure. An oven-dried 25 mL
round-bottomed flask with a magnetic stirring bar was charged with CuI
nanoparticles (1.25 mol %), K2CO3 (0.1662 g, 1.2 mmol),
nitrogencontaining heterocycle (1.2 mmol)/phenol (1.2 mmol), aryl
chloride (1.0 mmol), and DMF (1 mL) under air. The reaction mixture was
stirred for 30 min at room temperature and then transferred to a
preheated oil bath at 110 °C. At the end of the reaction, as judged by
TLC, the reaction mixture was then cooled to room temperature, diluted
with 2-3 mL of EtOAc, and centrifuged to remove the catalyst, and the
catalyst was further washed with 5-10 mL of EtOAc to make it free from
organic matter. The combined organic extracts were then concentrated
under reduced pressure, and the resulting residue was purified by column
chromatography on silica gel (60-120) using hexane/ethyl acetate (80:20)
eluent to provide the desired N-arylated/ O-arylated product. The
catalyst was oven-dried at 65 °C for 2 h and reused.
2-methoxy-1-phenoxybenzene (Table 4, Entry 5): Colourless oil, yield 90
%. 1H NMR (400 MHz, CDCl3, ppm): δ 3.68 (s, 3H), 6.49-6.51 (m, 3H),
6.52-6.60 (m, 1H), 6.85-6.90 (m, 1H), 7.05-7.10 (m, 1H), 7.26-7.31 (m,
2H); 13C NMR (100 MHz, CDCl3, ppm): δ 56.1, 112.9, 117.3, 121.1, 122.2,
122.6, 124.6, 129.6, 145.2, 151.6, 158.0. EIMS: m/z = 200 (M+).

$DATUM additional potassium carbonate (1.5 equiv) was added followed by phenol
(1.2 equiv) and stirring was continued for 24h. The resulting suspension
was filtered through a pad of Celite with aid of AcOEt, the filtrate was
diluted with additional AcOEt and was washed with brine and 10% HCl. The
aqueous layer was back-extracted with AcOEt and the combined organic
layers were washed with brine (3x), dried (MgSO4), filtered and
concentrated in vacuo. An orange oil was obtained, which was purified by
flash chromatography (Hexane/AcOEt 9:1) to render compound 36. Thick
yellow oil, yield 90%.

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM 3-Methyl-5-(2-phenoxy-4-trifluoromethyl-phenoxy)-phenol Example 63, step
A intermediate (7.0 g, 16.0 mmol), phenol (3.0 g, 32.0 mol), cesium
carbonate (10.43 g, 32.0 mol), and 2,2,6,6-tetramethyl-3,5-heptanedione
(0.74 g, 4.01 mmol) in 1-methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (70 mL) is purged with
N2, and then copper (I) chloride (0.79 g, 7.98 mmol) is added. The
reaction mixture is heated to 120°C for 20 hours under N2. The mixture is
diluted with water and extracted with Et2O. The organic layer is dried
(Na2SO4), and the solvent is removed in vacuo to afford crude product
that is absorbed on silica gel and purified by flash chromatography using
14/1 hexanes/ethyl acetate to afford 5.30 g (74%) product. Rf = 0.48 (4/1
hexanes/ethyl acetate) A mixture of 5.30 g of obtained above and 10% Pd/C
(2.50 g) in ethyl acetate (150 mL) is purged with N2 and then H2, and the
mixture is stirred under a H2 balloon at rt. Upon completion of the
reaction, the mixture is filtered through hyflo, and the solvent is
removed in vacuo to afford crude product that is purified by flash
chromatography using 5/1 hexanes/ethyl acetate to afford 3.83 g (90%) of
the title compound.
3-Methyl-5-(2-phenoxy-4-trifluoromethyl-phenoxy)-phenol, yield 3.83 g,
90% Rf = 0.28 (4/1 hexanes/ethyl acetate). 1H NMR (400 MHz, CDCl3); MS
(ES+) m/z mass calculated for C20H15F3O3 360, found 359 (M - 1, 100%).

$DATUM Reaction of [OsH(=C=C=CPh2)(CH3CN)2(PiPr3)2]BF4 with Phenol: Formation of
[OsH(OPh)( (CCH=CPh2)(CH3CN)(PiPr3)2]BF4 (3). A green solution of1 (260
mg, 0.298 mmol) in 10 mL of dichloromethane was treated with phenol (31
mg, 0.328 mmol). After the mixture was stirred for 30 min at room
temperature, it was filtered through Celite and the filtrate was
evaporated. The addition of diethyl ether afforded a red solid, which was
washed with a mixture of diethyl ether/pentane (1:3) and dried in vacuo.
[OsH(OPh)((CCH=CPh2)(CH3CN)(PiPr3)2]BF4 (3) Yield: 250 mg (90%) Anal.

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: 3. General Procedure for the Synthesis of
Diaryl Ethers 3 To a suspension of t-BuOK (1.1 equiv, 43 mg, 0.37 mmol)
in THF (1.5 mL) was added phenol 1 (1.0 equiv, 0.34 mmol) at 0 °C and the
reaction was left to stir at this temperature for 15 min. Diaryliodonium
salt 2 (1.2 equiv, 0.40 mmol) was added in one portion and the reaction
was stirred at rt or in an oil bath preheated to 40 °C and until TLC
indicated complete consumption of 1 (see Table 1). The reaction was then
quenched with H2O at 0 °C, the organic phase was separated and the water
phase was extracted with dichloromethane (3×10 mL). The combined organic
phases were dried (Na2SO4) and concentrated in vacuo. The crude material
was purified by flash chromatography (pentane:Et2O 100:1 → 25:1) to give
pure diaryl ether 3. 3-Trifluoromethylphenyl(phenyl) ether (3b), yield
90%. 1H NMR (400 MHz, CDCl3) δ 7.46-7.32 (m, 4H), 7.26-7.22 (m, 1H),
7.20-7.13 (m, 2H), 7.07-7.00 (m, 2H); 13C NMR (100 MHz, CDCl3) δ 158.0,
156.3, 132.4 (q, 2JF-C, J = 32.7 Hz), 130.4, 130.2, 124.3, 123.9 (q,
1JF-C = 272.4 Hz), 121.7, 121.7, 119.7 (q, 3JF-C = 3.8 Hz), 119.6, 115.4
(q, 3JF-C = 3.8 Hz); HRMS (EI): calcd for C13H9F3O [M]: 238.0605; found
238.0603.

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Typical Method 2 (TM2). A Schlenk tube
equipped with a stir bar under N2 was charged with BODIPY 1 (0.10 g, 0.42
mmol, 1 equiv) and CH3CN (6 mL). The mixture was purged with N2 for 5
min, whereupon CuTC (0.119 g, 0.63 mmol, 1.5 equiv) and the corresponding
alcohol or phenol was added (0.63 mmol, 1.5 equiv). The reaction mixture
was stirred for 5 min, upon which Na2CO3 (0.07 g, 0.63 mmol, 1.5 equiv)
was added. The Schlenk tube was immersed in a preheated oil bath at 55
&#x00B0;C and the stirring continued until the consumption of the
starting material. The solvent was removed in vacuo, and the crude
material was adsorbed in SiO2 gel. The product was purified by column
chromatography using a hexane/EtOAc gradient. For purposes of
characterization, the products were crystallized from CH2Cl2/hexanes.
BODIPY 7: following TM2; product (107.5 mg, 90%) obtained as a bright
yellow solid. Rf = 0.67 (30% EtOAc/hexanes); mp 129.8-131.4 &#x00B0;C; IR
(KBr; cm-1) 3122 (w), 1740 (w), 1573 (s), 1526 (m), 1486 (m), 1398 (s),

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General procedure for phosphite synthesis To a
stirred solution of 1.0 equivalent of 8 in toluene (30 mL/mmol) were
added 3.3 equivalents of triethyl amine and 1.1 equivalents of a 1M
solution of phosphorus trichloride in toluene. The mixture was stirred at
80 °C for 16 h. Then, 1.1 equivalents of the corresponding alcohol in
toluene (5 mL/mmol) were added and the reaction mixture was stirred at 80
°C for further 6 h. Diethyl ether (30 mL/mmol) was added and the mixture
was filtered. The filtrate was concentrated in vacuo and the residue
chromatographed on silica with mixtures of n-pentane and diethyl ether.

Claisen Rearrangement Reaction A two-necked round-bottomed flask was c Hα

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Hydrogenation of Substituted Arenes (Table 3).
Hydrogenation of arene was performed in a 100 mL stainless autoclave
fitted with a glass inner tube, in the presence of substrate (1 mmol) and
Rh/CNF-T (5 mg; S/C = 10,300) under H2 (initial pressure = 3 atm). The
chemical yield and the purity of the product were determined by capillary
GLC analysis using n-octane, n-decane, or hexamethylbenzene as an
internal standard. Entry 2: TC-17 (30 m), detection FID, column
temperature 140 °C, t R = 4.2 min (decane), 4.4 min (cyclohexanol), 4.8
min (cyclohexanone), 5.4 min (phenol).

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General Procedure for the Chlorination by
N-Chloro-2,3,4,4,5,6-hexachloro-2,5-dienylideneamine (3) To a
magnetically stirred solution of the phenols (phenol, o-cresol)
(0.74mmol) in the appropriate solvent (5 ml),
N-chloro-2,3,4,4,5,6-hexa-chlorocyclohexa-2,5-dienylideneamine (0.74mmol)
was added at the desired temperature (Tables 1-3). The progress of the
reaction was monitored by TLC (EtOAc: n-hexane, 3 :1). After completion
of the reaction, the solvent was evaporated in vacuo and the residue was
extracted by HCl 5% (2x15 ml) and washed with water (2 x 20 ml). The
organic phase dried (MgSO4) and evaporated in vacuo to produce the
chlorinated products. The ratio of chloro-phenols (ortho/para) was
determined by GC (SE 30 and OV225) using standard authentic samples. The
combined aqueous solution was made alkaline (NaOH 5%) and extracted by
ether (2 x20ml). The ethereal solution was dried (MgSO4) and evaporated
in vacuo to provide pentachloroaniline in ca. 70% yield. yield (para =
98.6%); yield (ortho = 1.4%)
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):NOTES
$DATUM regioselective, alternative reaction conditions gave lower yield

and highly regioselective chlorinating reagent

$DATUM General Procedure for the Photolysis of
4-N,N-diethylamino-3-nitrophenylazide (5) in the presence of Targeted
Functional groups. A solution of 20 mg of 5 and 200 mg of the molecule
containing the targeted functional group in acetonitrile (7 mL) was
flushed with nitrogen for 15 min and photolyzed for 4 h using 350 nm
light in a Rayonet Photochemical reactor. The crude photolysis mixture
was concentrated to dryness in vacuo, extracted with water and CH2Cl2,
dried over Na2SO4, leaving an oily residue, which was purified by
preparative TLC (hexane/dichloromethane) to give aniline 6 and addition
product as yellow oils. a) Irradiation in Presence of Phenol. Irradiation
in the presence of phenol afforded the phenol adduct in the 2-position 15
in 98% yield as an oil that had. 4-N,N-diethylamino-3-nitroaniline (6) 1H
NMR (300 MHz, CDCl3) δ 7.37-7.29 (m, 2H), 7.18 (d, J = 9 Hz, 1H), 7.09
(t, J = 7.2, Hz, 1H), 6.8 (d, J = 9 Hz, 1H), 6.91 (dd, J = 7.2, 0.9 Hz,
2H), 4.3 (s, NH2), 2.9 (q, J = 7.2 Hz, 4H), 0.9 (t, J = 7.2 Hz, 6H); 13C
NMR (75.5 MHz, CDCl3) δ 171.4, 156.44, 139.1, 138.4, 132.6, 129.39,
122.87, 122.63, 114.66, 49.36, 12.93; HRMS calcd for C16H19N3O3 (M + H)
302.14989, found 302.150467.

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM Phenol Nitration The catalyst is introduced into 8M HNO3 at a weight
ratio of 3:7 and stirred for 2 h at room temperature. On filtration the
catalyst is dried in the air. The content of the nitric acid adsorbed on
silica is determined by titration of the filtrate with an NaOH solution.
The acid used in the reaction is taken in a 110% excess of the
theoretical amount needed. The catalyst (1 g) with the adsorbed HNO3 and
CH2Cl2 (45 mL) were placed in the flask. Then 0.18 g (2.0 mmol) phenol
was added. The reaction is allowed to proceed for 3 min at room
temperature. On completion of the reaction the catalyst is filtered off
and washed with a little CH2Cl2, which was added to the filtrate. The
reaction products are analyzed by GLC. o-nitrophenol; p-nitrophenol,
yield 99% (8:92).
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):NOTES
$DATUM regioselective, optimization study, optimized on catalyst, other
catalysts gave poorer product distributions

$DATUM The oxidation reactions were carried out in a 25 mL thermostated (ca. 25
°C) Carius tube connected with a large reservoir containing oxygen at 101
KPa and under magnetic stirring. In a typical run, phenol (940 mg, 10
mmol), pyridine (2.4 g, 30 mmol), and commercial or MVS copper (13 mg,
0.2 mmol) in 10 mL of methanol were reacted for 24 h with molecular
oxygen. The solvents were evaporated in vacuo, and the crude reaction was
purified by flash chromatography. The products were characterized by MS
and 1H NMR analysis, and the data were consistent with those reported in
the literature. 4,5-dimethoxy-1,2-benzoquinone, 1 (96%).
1-hydroxy-2-oxo-4,5,5-trimethoxycyclopent-3-ene-1-methylcarboxylate, 2
(4%).

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: 2.5 Typical Procedure for the Bromination of
Aromatics with NBS An aromatic compound (1.0 mmol), Ag/HMB (Ag: 2-4
mol%), NBS (1.1 mmol), and dichloroethane (DCE) (2.0 mL) were added in a
pressure tube with a magnetic stir bar, and the tube was kept at 25-100
°C for 16 h (see Table 2 for the detailed reaction conditions). After the
reaction was completed, the reaction mixture was added 100 μL hexadecane
(internal standard), and the Ag/HMB was separated by filtration. The
conversions and yields were determined by GC with an internal standard
(C16H34). Entry: 9; Yield: 100%; o/p=1:14.

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Typical Procedure for Bromination of Phenols
and Anilines with NBSac Catalyzed by Tungstophosphoric Acid NBSac was
prepared according to the literature procedure.[12] To a mixture of
3-methylphenol (0.108 g, 1 mmol) and H3PW12O40 (0.0116 g, 0.4 mol %) in
CH3CN (5 mL) at 0 °C, NBSac (0.294 g, 1 mmol) was added, and the mixture
was stirred. After completion of the reaction as indicated by TLC, the
solvent was evaporated. Column chromatography of the crude mixture on
silica gel using n-hexane-EtOAc (10:1) gave the para-bromo-meta-cresol
(0.159 g, 85% yield, Table 1, entry 3). (Table 2, Entry 1), yield 90%
(p), yield 6% (o). Mp: 66°C.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):NOTES
$DATUM green chemistry-catalyst, regioselective, immediate conversion, optimized
on catalyst loading, optimization study

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Catalyst synthesis: Two synthetic methods were
applied to obtain dimeric catalysts. As one method, the precatalyst
(R,R)-salen CoII and Lewis acid (2:1) was dissolved in methylene chloride
(MC) simultaneously at ambient temperature and stirred in open atmosphere
for 3 h. The color of the reaction mass changed from red to olive green.
The solvent was evaporated up to dryness under reduced pressure to offer
the dark brown solid powder. Then the catalyst was treated by NBS (2
equivalents based on Co unit) under stirring in THF for 2 h. The solvent
was evaporated and catalyst was purified by recrystallization in MC. In a
representative reaction of epichlorohydrin (ECH) and phenol (table 1,
entry 6), the catalyst (R,R)-2a (867 mg, 0.05 mmol, 0.5 mol%,),
tert-butyl methyl ether (TBME) and (±)-ECH (0.93 g, 10 mmol) were charged
in an oven dried 25 mL flask and the reaction mixture was stirred in open
atmosphere at ambient temperature. Phenol (0.42 g, 4.5 mmol 0.45 equiv.)
was added after complete dissolution of the catalyst. The resultant
solution was stirred for 9 h and monitored by chiral GC and HPLC. The
purification of the products was performed by flash column
chromatography. The products were identified/characterized by IR, 1H-NMR,
13C-NMR and found to be similar to that reported. Table 1 Entry 8, yield
95%, yield 28%.

product distribution and ee% depends on precatalyst/Lewis acid ratio

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Catalyst synthesis: Two synthetic methods were
applied to obtain dimeric catalysts. As one method, the precatalyst
(R,R)-salen CoII and Lewis acid (2:1) was dissolved in methylene chloride
(MC) simultaneously at ambient temperature and stirred in open atmosphere
for 3 h. The color of the reaction mass changed from red to olive green.
The solvent was evaporated up to dryness under reduced pressure to offer
the dark brown solid powder. Then the catalyst was treated by NBS (2
equivalents based on Co unit) under stirring in THF for 2 h. The solvent
was evaporated and catalyst was purified by recrystallization in MC. In a
representative reaction of epichlorohydrin (ECH) and phenol (table 1,
entry 6), the catalyst (R,R)-2a (867 mg, 0.05 mmol, 0.5 mol%,),
tert-butyl methyl ether (TBME) and (±)-ECH (0.93 g, 10 mmol) were charged
in an oven dried 25 mL flask and the reaction mixture was stirred in open
atmosphere at ambient temperature. Phenol (0.42 g, 4.5 mmol 0.45 equiv.)
was added after complete dissolution of the catalyst. The resultant
solution was stirred for 9 h and monitored by chiral GC and HPLC. The
purification of the products was performed by flash column
chromatography. The products were identified/characterized by IR, 1H-NMR,
13C-NMR and found to be similar to that reported. Table 1 Entry 10, yield
93%, yield 29%.
$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):NOTES
$DATUM regioselective, stereoselective, alternative reaction conditions for
catalyst formation shown, in-situ generated catalyst-stages 1 and 2,
product distribution and ee% depends on precatalyst/Lewis acid ratio

$DTYPE RXN:VAR(1):EXP_PROC
$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: Catalyst synthesis: Two synthetic methods were
applied to obtain dimeric catalysts. As one method, the precatalyst
(R,R)-salen CoII and Lewis acid (2:1) was dissolved in methylene chloride
(MC) simultaneously at ambient temperature and stirred in open atmosphere
for 3 h. The color of the reaction mass changed from red to olive green.
The solvent was evaporated up to dryness under reduced pressure to offer
the dark brown solid powder. Then the catalyst was treated by NBS (2
equivalents based on Co unit) under stirring in THF for 2 h. The solvent
was evaporated and catalyst was purified by recrystallization in MC. In a
representative reaction of epichlorohydrin (ECH) and phenol (table 1,
entry 6), the catalyst (R,R)-2a (867 mg, 0.05 mmol, 0.5 mol%,),
tert-butyl methyl ether (TBME) and (±)-ECH (0.93 g, 10 mmol) were charged
in an oven dried 25 mL flask and the reaction mixture was stirred in open
atmosphere at ambient temperature. Phenol (0.42 g, 4.5 mmol 0.45 equiv.)
was added after complete dissolution of the catalyst. The resultant
solution was stirred for 9 h and monitored by chiral GC and HPLC. The
purification of the products was performed by flash column
chromatography. The products were identified/characterized by IR, 1H-NMR,
13C-NMR and found to be similar to that reported. Table 1 Entry 12, yield
91%, yield 31%.

$DATUM General/Typical Procedure: General Procedure for the Preparation of 6. To
a stirred mixture of compound 3a (1 mmol) in PEG-400 (2 g) at room
temperature were added nucleophiles (1.5 mmol) and NaOtBu (1.5 mmol).
After the mixture was stirred at room temperature for 1.5 h (TLC
monitoring), the reaction mixture was treated with water, and extracted
with ethyl acetate, the organiclayers were dried over Na2SO4. The crude
product was purified by flash chromatography (petroleum ether/ethyl
acetate =10:1) to give pure products 6 as colorless oil. Compound: 7a,
Yield: 90 %, Compound: 2, Reactant: 3a. 7a: M.p. 93-94 °C. 1HNMR (400
MHz, CDCl3) δ= 2.44 (s, 3H), 6.96-7.70 (m, 9H). 13CNMR (100 MHz, CDCl3)
δ= 21.6, 122.3, 127.0, 128.4, 129.5, 129.6, 132.4, 125.2, 149.6.
